قوله : (والسلب للكل إن لم ينفل) أي لا يختص به القاتل عندنا لأنه مأخوذ بقوة الجيش فيكون غنيمة فيقسم بينهم قسمة الغنائم كما نطق به النص وقال عليه السلام الحبيب بن أبي سلمة ليس لك من سلب قتيلك إلا ما طابت به نفس إمامك. وأما قوله عليه السلام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه» (۱) فيحتمل نصب الشرع ويحتمل التنفيل فنحمله على الثاني لما روينا قوله : (وهو) مركبه وثيابه وسلاحه وما معه) أي السلب ما ذكر للعرف. وفي المغرب : السلب المسلوب وعن الليث والأزهري : كل ما على الإنسان من اللباس فهو سلب وللفقهاء فيه كلام .اهـ. وفي القاموس السلب بالتحريك ما يسلب وجمعه أسلاب ودخل في مركبه ما كان عليه من سرج وآلة وما مع المقتول شامل لما كان في وسطه أو على دابته وما عدا ذلك مما هو مع غلامه أو في بيته أو في خيمته فليس بسلب. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان السلب عند المشرك عارية من صبي أو امرأة لأنه يستغنم مالهما كمال البالغ، وما إذا كان السلب ملكاً لمسلم دخل دارهم بأمان فغصبه المشرك المقتول لأنه ملكه بالاستيلاء فانقطع ملك المسلم عنه . ولو أخذ المشركون سلب المقتول ثم انهزموا فهو غنيمة ولا شيء للقاتل لأنهم ملكوه بالاستيلاء فبطل ملك القاتل ثم ملكه الغزاة وإن لم يدر أنهم أخذوه، فإن كان منزوعاً عنه فهو فيء لإثبات يدهم عليه بالنزع وإلا فهو للقاتل وإن جره المشركون أو حملوه على دابته وعليها سلاحه بخلاف ما إذا حملوا أسلحتهم وأمتعتهم عليها فإنه فيء. ولو وجد على دابة بعدما سار العسكر مرحلة أو مرحلتين ولا يدري أكان أحد في يد أو لا فهو للقاتل قياساً لا استحساناً ولو قال من قتل قتيلاً فله فرسه فقتل راجل راجلاً ومع غلامه فرسه قائم بجنبه بين الصفين يكون للقاتل فرسه إذا كان فرسه مع . غلامه بقرب منه لأن مقصود الإمام قتل من كان متمكناً من القتال فارساً وهذا كذلك، وإن لم يكن بجنبه في الصف فلا يكون له. ولو قتل مشركاً على برذون كان له لأنه يسمى فارساً، ولو كان على حمار أو بغل أو حمل لا يستحق السلب لأن راكب هذه الأشياء لا فارساً ولذا لا يسمى يستحق سهم الفارس؛ كذا في المحيط وبه علم أن ما ذكره الشارح عن المحيط بأنه قال الإمام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه سبق قلم، وإنما المذكور في المحيط فله فرسه والدليل عليه أنه قوله : (سبق (قلم قال الرملي : أي من بعض النساخ والذي في نسخنا من الزيلعي فله فرسه كما في المحيط
His statement: (And the salb is for everyone if he did not make nafal) meaning it is not exclusive to the killer according to us because it is taken by the strength of the army, so it is ghanimah and is divided among them as ghanimah is divided, as the text states. The Prophet ﷺ said to al-Hubāb ibn Abī Salama: 'You do not have from the salb of your killed except what your imam is pleased with.' As for his saying, 'Whoever kills a killed one gets his salb,' it is possible it was established by the Law or it could be nafal, so we carry it on the second because of what we narrated. His statement: (And it is) his mount, clothes, weapon, and what is with him. i.e., salb is what is mentioned according to custom. In al-Mughrib: al-salb is the plundered item. And from al-Layth and al-Azhari: everything on a person of clothing is salb, and the jurists differ. In al-Qāmūs: al-salb (with tahrīk) is what is plundered, plural aslāb. Included in his mount is what is on it of saddle and equipment, and what is with the killed includes what is in his waist or on his animal, and other than that which is with his servant or in his house or tent is not salb. [The rule] is absolute and includes if the salb was with the polytheist as a loan from a boy or woman, because their property is taken as booty like that of an adult; and if the salb was owned by a Muslim who entered their land with aman and the killed polytheist usurped it, because he owns it by domination, so the Muslim's ownership ceases. If the polytheists took the salb of the killed and then were defeated, it is ghanimah and nothing for the killer because they owned it by domination, so the killer's ownership is nullified, then the warriors own it even if they did not know they took it. If it was stripped from him, it is fay' because they placed their hand on it by stripping; otherwise it is for the killer. If the polytheists dragged it or loaded it on his animal while his weapon is on it, contrary to if they load their own weapons and goods on it, then it is fay'. If found on an animal after the army marched one or two stages and it is not known whether anyone had it, it is for the killer by qiyas not istihsan. If he said, 'Whoever kills a killed one gets his horse,' and a foot soldier kills a foot soldier while with his servant his horse stands beside him between the two lines, he gets the horse if his horse is near him because the imam's purpose is killing those who are capable of fighting as a horseman, and this is such. If he is not beside him in the line, he does not get it. If he kills a polytheist on a horse (baradhūn) he gets it because he is called a horseman; if on a donkey or mule or baggage animal, he does not deserve the salb because the rider of such things is not a horseman and does not deserve the horseman's share. So in al-Muhīt, and from it it is known that what the commentator mentioned from al-Muhīt that the imam said 'Whoever kills a killed one gets his salb' is a slip of the pen; what is mentioned in al-Muhīt is 'gets his horse', and the evidence is... His statement: (slip of the pen) al-Ramlī said: i.e., from some copyists, and in our copies from al-Zaylaʿī 'gets his horse' as in al-Muhīt.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-ruling passage. It defines 'salb' (the spoils taken from a killed enemy) and clarifies its distribution in Hanafi fiqh. The matn states that the salb is for all the soldiers, not exclusively for the killer, unless the imam makes it nafal (extra reward) for the killer. The commentator explains that the salb is considered ghanimah because it was acquired through the collective strength of the army, and it is divided accordingly. Two hadiths are cited: one where the Prophet said to al-Hubāb that he does not own the salb except by the imam's permission, and another where the Prophet said 'Whoever kills a killed one gets his salb.' The Hanafis interpret the second as nafal, not as an absolute right, based on the first hadith. Then the commentator defines 'salb' according to custom: it includes the enemy's mount, clothes, weapons, and what is with him (such as items on his person or animal). It does not include items with his servant or in his home. Various scenarios are discussed: if the salb was borrowed from a child or woman, it is still ghanimah; if it was owned by a Muslim who entered with aman and was usurped, the killer does not get it; if the polytheists take the salb and then are defeated, it becomes ghanimah again. The passage also rules on specific cases like finding a horse after marching, and the imam's statement about giving the horse to the killer. A textual correction is noted: the proper version in al-Muhīt is 'gets his horse', not 'gets his salb'.

Key Terms
سلب (salb): The belongings on the person of a killed enemy: mount, clothes, weapons, and what is with him.
فيء (fay'): Booty taken from the enemy without direct combat (e.g., when the enemy flees and leaves items).
تنفيل (tafnīl): The act of the imam granting extra reward (nafal) to a soldier from the booty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه'
B) 'من قتل قتيلاً فله فرسه'
C) 'من قتل قتيلاً فله مركبه'
D) 'من قتل قتيلاً فله سلاحه'

Key Takeaway
The accurate textual transmission is vital: the imam’s nafal is specifically for the horse, reinforcing that general salb remains collective property.

The Escaped Slave: Fay' or Ghanimah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on escaped slave's status and master's right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the escaped slave and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each.

Core Idea
A slave escaping from dar al-harb with enemy property triggers a dispute: is it fay' or ghanimah? The timing of the master's appearance decides the price.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani concerning a slave who escapes enemy territory with stolen property and is seized by a Muslim. The core question is whether the slave is treated as fay' (community property) or ghanimah (spoils requiring khums), and how that affects the original master's right to reclaim him. By understanding this dispute, you will see how Hanafi jurists use qiyas and retraction to refine rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
The passage contains Abu Hanifa's view, Muhammad's initial view, and Muhammad's retracted view. List them clearly.
2
Understand the legal basis for each
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to equate the slave to fay'; Muhammad first treats it like any captured property; later he analogizes to ghanimah.
Qiyas is explicit in the text: 'في قياس قول أبي حنيفة'.
3
Apply the key variable: timing of master's appearance
Muhammad's retracted view hinges on whether the master appears before or after khums is taken. Before: free; after: pay price.
4
Derive the practical consequences
Under Abu Hanifa: master always free. Under Muhammad (retracted): conditional on khums. Under Muhammad (first): master always pays.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Note the citation from al-Multaqat
The passage ends with a conflicting narration that the slave is returned free or even freed, showing a range of opinion within the school.
This indicates the issue remained debated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب استيلاء الكفار
أسره العدوّ وأحرز بدارهم ثم انفلت منهم وأخذ شيئاً من أموالهم وخرج هارباً إلى دار الإسلام فأخذه مسلم ثم جاء مولاه لم يأخذه منه إلا بالقيمة في قول محمد، وما في يده من المال فهو لمن أخذه ولا سبيل للمولى عليه وأما في قياس قول أبي حنيفة فإن المولى يأخذ العبد بغير شيء لأنه لما دخل دار الإسلام صار فيئاً لجماعة المسلمين يأخذه الإمام ويرفع خمسه ويقسم أربعة أخماسه بين الغانمين، ثم رجع محمد عن قوله وقال : إذا أخذه مسلم فهو غنيمة آخذه وأخمسه إذا لم يحضر المولى واجعل أربعة أخماس العبد والمال الذي معه للآخذ، فإن جاء مولاه بعد ذلك أخذه بالقيمة، وإن جاء مولاه قبل أن يخمس أخذه بغير شيء اهـ. وفي الملتقط : عبد أسره أهل الحرب والحقوه بدارهم ثم أبق منهم يرد إلى سيده وفي رواية يعتق اهـ .
Chapter on Seizing of Unbelievers. The enemy captured him and secured him in their land, then he escaped from them and took something of their property and fled to Dar al-Islam, then a Muslim took him, then his master came; he does not take him from him except with the price according to Muhammad's statement, and what is in his hand of property belongs to the one who took it and the master has no claim over it. As for the analogy of Abu Hanifa's statement, the master takes the slave without anything because when he entered Dar al-Islam he became fay' for the entire Muslim community; the Imam takes it and sets aside its khums and divides four-fifths among the warriors. Then Muhammad retracted his statement and said: If a Muslim takes him, it is ghanimah; I take it and pay khums on it if the master is not present, and I make four-fifths of the slave and the property with him for the taker. If his master comes after that, he takes him with the price, and if his master comes before he pays khums, he takes him without anything. End. And in Al-Multaqat: A slave captured by the people of war and they joined him to their land, then he ran away from them, he is returned to his master, and in one narration he becomes free. End.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of a slave captured by harbi enemies who then escapes taking enemy property and reaches Dar al-Islam only to be seized by a Muslim. The original master then appears. Imam Muhammad initially ruled that the master can only reclaim the slave by paying the price (i.e., compensating the Muslim who took him), and that any property the slave stole from the enemy belongs to that Muslim taker. Abu Hanifa, by analogy (qiyas), held that the master takes the slave without any payment because upon entering Dar al-Islam the slave becomes fay' (booty without war) owned by the Muslim community; the Imam is supposed to take it, deduct the khums (one-fifth), and distribute the rest to the warriors. However, Muhammad later retracted his earlier view and adopted a detailed position: if a Muslim seizes the slave, it is treated as ghanimah (spoils of war) – the Muslim must pay khums on it if the master does not appear, and the taker gets four-fifths of the slave and the property. If the master comes after the khums has been set aside, the master takes the slave by paying the price; if the master comes before the khums is paid, the master takes the slave without paying anything. The passage ends by citing Al-Multaqat, which states that a captured slave who escapes from dar al-harb is returned to his master without any payment, and in one narration he becomes free. The teacher explains that the ruling depends on when the master appears and whether khums has been taken, reflecting the Hanafi school's nuanced approach to property rights in the context of jihad and booty.

Key Terms
فيء (fay'): Property taken from unbelievers without warfare (e.g., when they flee or surrender peacefully).
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils taken by force from combatants during battle; one-fifth (khums) is set aside and the rest distributed among warriors.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here used by Abu Hanifa to equate the escaped slave to fay'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad's final (retracted) position, when does the original master take the escaped slave without paying anything?
A) If the master comes before the Muslim taker pays khums.
B) If the master comes after the khums has been set aside.
C) If the slave was captured without property.
D) If the Muslim taker is a relative of the master.

Key Takeaway
The master's right to reclaim an escaped slave in Dar al-Islam depends on the classification of the slave (fay' vs. ghanimah) and, in Muhammad's view, on the timing of the master's appearance relative to the payment of khums.

Rulings on the Harbi Convert and Killing Without a Guardian
Combines property and diyah rulings with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the property of a converted harbi and the diyah options for killing a Muslim without an heir, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for a foundling.

Core Idea
A harbi convert's young child is free and Muslim; deposits with protected persons remain his, other property is fay'.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains two connected but distinct sets of rulings: the status of a harbi who converts in dar al-harb and then enters dar al-Islam, and the diyah rules for killing a Muslim or a converted musta'min who has no individual heir. The commentary also addresses the foundling (laqit) and an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the applicability of qisas. Let us walk through the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases in the matn
The passage covers (a) the status of a harbi convert's young child and his deposited property, and (b) the diyah rules for killing a Muslim without a guardian or a converted musta'min. Recognize these as separate legal issues.
The matn begins with the convert's property rules, then shifts to diyah.
2
Analyze the harbi convert's child and property
The young child follows the better religion of the father and becomes free and Muslim. Deposits (wadi'ah) left with a Muslim or dhimmi remain the convert's property because those hands are protected. All other property becomes fay' (booty for the state) because the convert's own hand was not protected.
The distinction hinges on whether the property is in a protected hand (yad muhramah) or not.
3
Understand mistaken killing of one without a guardian
If a Muslim or a converted musta'min is killed by mistake and has no known heir, the killer's 'aqila must pay diyah, and the diyah is given to the Imam (public treasury). The 'aqila is responsible because the soul is inviolable.
This applies even if the victim has children in dar al-harb, as they cannot inherit due to dar al-harb status.
4
Examine intentional killing options
For intentional killing of one without an heir, the Imam has the choice between qisas (execution) or accepting diyah via conciliation with the killer's consent. The Imam cannot pardon because the right belongs to the public.
This is based on the hadith 'the sultan is the guardian of one who has no guardian.'
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the foundling
Abu Yusuf argues that qisas should not apply to a foundling because an heir is possible, creating shubhah (ambiguity). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the unknown potential heir is effectively non-existent, so the Imam can choose qisas. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the majority view.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Yusuf's view, only diyah or pardon; under the majority, the Imam can execute.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وارث عندنا. قوله : ماله في بيت المال ليصرف مصارفه لأن المصرح به لكن بعد التأني) بالتاء المثناة والهمزة والنون المشددة أي التمهل. يوضع
His young child is free and Muslim. Whatever he deposited with a Muslim or a dhimmi is for him, and other than that is fay'. Whoever kills a believer by mistake who has no guardian, or a harbi who came to us under aman and then became Muslim, his diyah is on his 'aqila for the Imam. In intentional killing, either execution or diyah, not pardon. In al-Binaya: (If he becomes Muslim there and comes to us, and we overcome them, his young child is free and Muslim, and his deposit with a Muslim or dhimmi is for him, and other than that is fay'.) This is an explanation of the ruling of the property of a harbi who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb and comes, leaving his wealth and children, then we overcome the people of war. As for the young child, he follows his father to us as a Muslim at the time he became Muslim, since the dar is one, so he is free and Muslim. What was deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi is for him because it is in a protected hand, and his hand is like his hand. Other than that is fay'. As for the wife and adult children, according to what we said. As for wealth in the hand of a harbi, because it did not become inviolable, since the hand of a harbi is not a protected hand. And it includes other things like a usurped property in the hand of a Muslim or dhimmi, so it is fay' due to lack of representation; thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (Whoever kills a believer by mistake who has no guardian, or a harbi who came to us under aman and then became Muslim, his diyah is on his 'aqila by mistake, so it is considered like other inviolable souls. The meaning of his statement 'for the Imam' is that a soul whose right is with the Imam) because he killed an inviolable soul, so he takes it because he has no heir — not that the Imam owns it, but it is placed in the public treasury, which is the purpose of mentioning it here. Otherwise, the ruling of mistaken killing is known, and therefore he did not mention the expiation because it will come in the chapter on injuries. Because he has no guardian. If he had limited it to the first case, it would have included the second because when a harbi becomes Muslim in our land and has no heir, he has no guardian even if he has children in dar al-harb. His statement: (In intentional killing, either execution or diyah, not pardon) means if someone kills by intention a person who has no guardian, the Imam has a choice: if he wishes, he may execute him; if he wishes, he may take the diyah for the public treasury because the soul is inviolable, the killing is intentional, and the guardian is known, which is the sultan because he is the guardian of anyone who has no guardian, as in the hadith. Taking the diyah is by way of conciliation with the consent of the killer because the requirement of intentional killing is exactly retaliation. This is because even if the diyah is more beneficial for the Muslims than his execution, it may be that executing him brings another benefit in deterring Muslims from killing. The Imam does not have the right to pardon because the right belongs to the general public, and his guardianship is supervisory, and such persons are not deterred by consideration from dropping their right without compensation. His speech includes the foundling: if he is killed by mistake, the diyah is for the Imam, whether the finder or someone else kills him. If he is killed intentionally, there is a choice, as in the book, and this is their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) view. Abu Yusuf said: He does not have the right to retaliation because the foundling is rarely free from an heir, or it is possible, so there is ambiguity, which drops it. Their (Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad's) evidence: The unknown person who cannot be reached is not a guardian because the deceased does not benefit from him, so he becomes like non-existent, so the guardianship transfers to the sultan. His statement: (If he had limited it to the first case, etc.) is examined in al-Nahr after his saying 'or kill a harbi' meaning who has no guardian, and by this the topics of the two cases differ. In the gloss of Abu al-Su'ud from al-Hamawi: There is consideration in the examination because the existence of a harbi in dar al-harb is like non-existence unless he comes and claims, then the wealth is for him, so it must be verified. His statement: (His inheritance is for the public treasury) means the public treasury is not an heir in our school. His statement: (His wealth is in the public treasury to be spent in its channels because it is explicitly stated but after waiting) with the letters taa and hamza and shadda, i.e., deliberation. It is placed.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the chapter of al-Musta'min. It covers two main issues: (1) The status of a harbi who converts to Islam in dar al-harb and then comes to dar al-Islam, and (2) the diyah rules for killing a Muslim or a converted musta'min who has no guardian. On the first issue, the young child of such a convert is automatically free and Muslim because the child follows the better religion of the father, and the dar is considered one for this ruling. Any deposits (wadi'ah) the harbi had with a Muslim or dhimmi remain his property because those hands are protected; all other property left behind becomes fay' (booty for the Muslim state). On the second issue, killing a Muslim or a musta'min who converted by mistake requires diyah (blood money) on the killer's 'aqila (tribal or contractual supporters), which is paid to the Imam (public treasury) since there is no individual heir. For intentional killing, the Imam has the option of either executing the killer (qisas) or accepting diyah via conciliation with the killer's consent, but he cannot pardon fully because the right belongs to the public. The commentary also addresses a foundling (laqit): if killed by mistake, diyah to Imam; if killed intentionally, same option. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf argues that qisas should not apply to a foundling because an heir is possible, creating ambiguity; but the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that unknown potential heirs are like non-existent, so the Imam acts as guardian. The passage emphasizes that the public treasury (bayt al-mal) is not an heir but a recipient for the benefit of Muslims, and funds are placed after deliberation.

Key Terms
المستأمن (al-musta'min): A non-Muslim who enters dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) for a temporary period.
الحربي (al-harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under a peace treaty and lives in dar al-harb (land of war).
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The tribal or contractual supporters (like 'asaba) who are liable to pay diyah in cases of accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim kills a foundling by mistake. According to the Hanafi school, who receives the diyah?
A) The finder of the foundling
B) The public treasury (Imam)
C) The heirs of the foundling if discovered later
D) The killer's family

Key Takeaway
For a Muslim killed without an heir, the Imam has the choice of qisas or diyah in intentional killing, and diyah is paid to the public treasury in mistaken killing.

Actions and Words That Constitute Kufr
States that actions showing contempt for religion are kufr, and warns against dismissing takfir as mere threat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on actions and words that constitute kufr and identify the proof from the sources cited.

Core Idea
Contempt for religion, even in jest, constitutes actual apostasy in Hanafi law.

This passage addresses a critical issue: when does a Muslim's action or word remove them from Islam? The Hanafi school holds that any act or word showing contempt (istikhkaf) for religion, such as praying without wudu deliberately or mocking religious practices, causes apostasy—even without inner belief. However, the passage also warns that only the rulings of mujtahids are authoritative for takfir; statements from later followers cannot be relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is any action or word showing contempt for Islam. The ruling is that it constitutes kufr (apostasy).
Examples include praying without wudu deliberately or persisting in abandoning a sunnah out of contempt.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the statements of the mujtahids as recorded in al-Musayarah, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Bazzaziyyah.
These books are authoritative in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof shows that such acts indicate istikhfaf (contempt), and contempt for religion is equivalent to kufr.
The phrase 'considering the respect that negates contempt' is key.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later followers downplay these rulings as mere threats, but the mufta bihi is real takfir.
Only mujtahid opinions are reliable for takfir.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa relies on the rulings of the mujtahids, not the opinions of non-mujtahids.
The passage explicitly states that what is from the mujtahid is on its reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المسايرة : ولاعتبار التعظيم المنافي للاستخفاف كفر الحنفية بألفاظ كثيرة وأفعال تصدر من المتهتكين لدلالتها على الاستخفاف بالدين كالصلاة بلا وضوء عمداً بل بالمواظبة على ترك سنة استخفافاً بها بسبب أنه إنما فعلها النبي وزيادة أو استقباحها كمن استقبح من آخر جعل بعض العمامة تحت حلقه أو إحفاء شاربه .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : ومن هزل بلفظ كفر ارتد وإن لم يعتقده للاستخفاف فهو ككفر العناد والألفاظ التي يكفر بها تعرف في الفتاوى اهـ. فهذا وما قبله صريح في أن ألفاظ التكفير المعروفة في الفتاوى موجبة للردة عن الإسلام حقيقة. وفي البزازية : ويحكى عن بعض من لا سلف له أنه كان يقول ما ذكر في الفتاوى أنه يكفر بكذا وكذا فذاك للتخويف والتهويل لا لحقيقة الكفر وهذا كلام باطل إلى آخره. والحق أن ما عن المجتهد فهو على حقيقته، وأما ما ثبت عن غيره فلا يفتي به في مثل التكفير ولذا قال في فتح القدير من باب البغاة : إن الذي صح عن المجتهدين في الخوارج عدم تكفيرهم ويقع في كلام أهل المذهب تكفير كثير لكن ليس من كلام الفقهاء الذين هم المجتهدون بل من غيرهم ولا عبرة بغير الفقهاء اهـ .
And in al-Musayarah: Considering the respect that negates contempt, kufr is affirmed by many words and actions that issue from the shameless, because they indicate contempt for religion, such as praying without wudu deliberately, even persisting in abandoning a sunnah out of contempt because of the claim that the Prophet only did it as an addition, or considering it ugly like one who considers it ugly for another to place part of the turban under his chin or to shave his mustache. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: Whoever jokes with a word of kufr apostatizes even if he does not believe it, due to contempt; it is like kufr of obstinacy. The words that result in kufr are known from the fatwa collections. End. So this and what preceded clearly shows that the famous words of takfir in the fatwa collections actually necessitate apostasy from Islam. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: It is narrated that some without predecessors would say that what is mentioned in the fatawa about apostasy due to certain words is only for intimidation and exaggeration, not actual apostasy. This is false speech. The truth is that what comes from the mujtahid is real, and what is established from others (non-mujtahids) should not be used for fatwa in matters like takfir. Hence in Fath al-Qadir from the chapter on rebels: What is authentically established from the mujtahids regarding the Khawarij is that they do not declare them disbelievers. And in the speech of many madhhab followers there is much takfir, but it is not from the speech of the fiqh scholars who are the mujtahids, but from others, and others are not considered.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that addresses the legal principle that words or actions showing contempt for religion constitute actual apostasy, not merely threats. The author cites two key sources: al-Musayarah and Fath al-Qadir. The first states that Hanafis rule kufr for actions that show contempt, such as praying without wudu deliberately, or persisting in abandoning a sunnah due to contempt (e.g., thinking the Prophet only did it as an extra), or finding fault with religious practices like wearing part of the turban under the chin or shaving the mustache. The second source (Fath al-Qadir) states that even joking with a word of kufr constitutes apostasy because of contempt, even without belief, akin to kufr of obstinacy. The author then emphasizes that the takfir expressions found in fatwa collections are real and not mere intimidation. He refutes the claim of some who dismiss these rulings as exaggeration. However, he cautions that only the rulings of mujtahids are authoritative; statements from non-mujtahids within the madhhab should not be relied upon for takfir. He gives the example of the Khawarij: the mujtahids (like Abu Hanifa) did not declare them disbelievers, even though some later Hanafis did. So we must distinguish between the fatwa of the mujtahid and the opinions of later followers.

Key Terms
الاستخفاف (al-istikhfaf): Treating religion with contempt or mockery
التكفير (al-takfir): Declaring someone to be a disbeliever

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is a sinner but still a Muslim
B) He commits apostasy because the action indicates contempt
C) He must repeat the prayer with wudu
D) It is permissible if he does not believe it is obligatory

Key Takeaway
Actions or words showing contempt for religion constitute real apostasy in Hanafi law, based on the rulings of the mujtahids.

When Does a Prayer Violation Become Kufr?
List of prayer violations with kufr implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the adopted Hanafi ruling on which deliberate prayer violations cause kufr and explain the role of istikhfaf in the disagreement.

Core Idea
Only praying without wudu intentionally causes kufr, and only when no contempt is present.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses a delicate question: when does a deliberate violation of prayer obligations become an act of kufr (apostasy)? The Hanafi school distinguishes between different violations based on the presence of contempt (istikhfaf) and the specific act. We will parse the text to understand the adopted ruling and the scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts listed
Read the passage and list the four deliberate prayer violations mentioned: abandoning prayer, praying to wrong qibla, praying in a najis garment, and praying without wudu.
2
Determine the ruling for each
The text states 'المأخوذ به الكفر في الأخير فقط' — the adopted view is that kufr applies only to the last case (praying without wudu).
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the phrase 'وقيل لا في الكل' — some scholars say kufr in none of them, while others say in all three. The disagreement is among Hanafis themselves.
The phrase 'الكفر في الأخير فقط' is the mufta bihi.
4
Understand the condition of istikhfaf
The disagreement applies only when there is no contempt (استخفاف) for religion. If contempt is present, all agree it becomes kufr.
Contempt changes the ruling drastically.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
Thus, the operative ruling: a person who deliberately prays without wudu without contempt is considered a kafir by the adopted view. For other acts, kufr is not declared without contempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبترك الصلاة متعمداً غيرنا وللقضاء وغير خائف من العقاب وبصلاته لغير القبلة متعمداً أو في ثوب نجس أو بغير وضوء عمداً والمأخوذ به الكفر في الأخير فقط وقيل لا في الكل، ومحل الاختلاف إذا لم يكن استخفافاً بالدين لا بسجوده بغير طهارة.
And by deliberately abandoning prayer, other than us? and for qada? and not fearing punishment, and by praying towards other than the qibla deliberately, or in a najis garment, or without wudu intentionally. And the ruling of kufr is adopted in the last only, and it is said: not in all. And the locus of disagreement is when there is no contempt for religion, not by his prostrating without purity.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage lists actions related to prayer that may cause apostasy. Deliberately abandoning prayer (assuming it is not due to denial of its obligation) is kufr, according to some. Praying towards a wrong direction intentionally, praying in a najis garment, or praying without wudu are all considered. The text says that the accepted ruling is that kufr occurs only in the last case (praying without wudu intentionally). However, some say kufr occurs in all cases. The disagreement applies when there is no element of contempt (istikhfaf) for religion. If someone prostrates without purity out of contempt, that is clearly kufr.

Key Terms
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Contempt; an attitude of disrespect towards religious duties.
المأخوذ به (al-ma'khudh bihi): The adopted position; the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Praying without facing the qibla.
B) Abandoning prayer deliberately.
C) Praying without wudu intentionally.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Only praying without wudu intentionally results in kufr by the adopted Hanafi view, and this applies only when there is no contempt for religion.

Apostasy and Acts of Worship: Nullification and Persistence of Obligations
Rulings on apostasy's effect on waqf and pre-existing obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which acts of worship are nullified by apostasy and which obligations persist, applying the Hanafi principle that disbelievers are not addressed by the Shari'a.

Core Idea
Apostasy nullifies pious acts like waqf but does not erase past sins; missed worship from before apostasy must be made up.

Apostasy (ridda) has profound effects on a person's religious obligations. This ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies what happens to acts of worship performed before apostasy and what remains due after returning to Islam. Understanding this reveals a key Hanafi principle: disbelievers are not addressed by the Shari'a's detailed commands, yet past sins persist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
The passage addresses two separate issues: (1) the fate of a waqf made while Muslim, and (2) the obligation to make up missed prayers and fasts from before apostasy, as well as the non-obligation of acts during apostasy.
2
Analyse the ruling on waqf
The waqf is completely nullified by apostasy and does not revive upon return to Islam; a new waqf must be made. If the apostate dies or leaves, the waqf property becomes inheritable.
This is based on the principle that an act of piety (qurba) cannot persist with apostasy.
3
Analyse the ruling on pre-apostasy missed obligations
Missed prayers and fasts from before apostasy remain a liability (ma'khudh bihi). The sin of missing them persists, so they must be made up after returning to Islam.
The proof is the persistence of sin (ma'siya) even after apostasy.
4
Understand the non-obligation during apostasy
No acts of worship become obligatory during apostasy itself because, according to the Hanafi school, disbelievers are not addressed by the commands of Shari'a (khitab al-kuffar bi al-shara'i').
This is a key difference from the Shafi'i school, which holds that disbelievers are addressed.
5
Connect the rulings to the underlying principle
The Hanafi position rests on two pillars: (a) sins and obligations incurred before apostasy survive because they are fixed liabilities; (b) no new obligations arise during apostasy because the divine address does not apply to a disbeliever.
The principle is talil (reasoning) based on the nature of khitab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤاخذ بعقوبة الكفر الأول والثاني وهو قول الفقيه أبي الليث ومن العبادات التي بطلت بردته وقفه الذي وقفه حال إسلامه، سواء كان على قربة ابتداء أو على ذريته ثم على المساكين لأنه قربة ولا بقاء لها مع وجود الردة، وإذا عاد مسلماً لا يعود وقفه إلا بتجديد منه. وإذا مات أو قتل أو لحق كان الوقف ميراثاً بين ورثته كما أوضحه الخصاف في آخر أوقافه. ومنها بقاء مع الردة ولذا قال في الخانية : إذا كان على المرتد قضاء صلوات أو صيامات تركها في الإسلام ثم أسلم قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : عليه قضاء ما ترك في الإسلام لأن ترك الصلاة والصيام معصية والمعصية تبقى بعد الردة .اهـ. ومنها أنه لا يجب عليه شيء من العبادات عندنا لعدم خطاب الكفار بالشرائع عندنا فلا يقضي ما فاته زمن ردته بعد إسلامه .
He is taken to account for the punishment of the first and second disbelief, and this is the statement of Abu al-Layth. Among the acts of worship nullified by his apostasy is his endowment (waqf) made while a Muslim, whether it was initially for a pious purpose or for his descendants then for the poor, because it is an act of piety and it does not persist with apostasy. If he returns as a Muslim, his endowment does not return except by his renewal. If he dies, is killed, or joins (enemy territory), the endowment becomes inheritance among his heirs, as clarified by al-Khassaf at the end of his book on endowments. Among them (rulings) is the persistence of sin with apostasy; hence al-Khaniyya states: If an apostate has to make up prayers or fasts that he missed in Islam, then becomes Muslim, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: He must make up what he missed in Islam because missing prayer and fasting is a sin, and sin remains after apostasy. End quote. Among them is that nothing of worship is obligatory upon him in our school because, in our view, disbelievers are not addressed by the divine laws; thus he does not make up what he missed during his apostasy after becoming Muslim.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It states that apostasy nullifies certain acts of worship, specifically a waqf made by the apostate while Muslim. The waqf is completely voided and does not return upon reversion to Islam unless the person makes a new waqf. Upon death or joining enemy territory, the waqf's assets become inheritable. However, obligations that existed before apostasy, such as missed prayers and fasts, remain due; the apostate must make them up after returning to Islam. This is because the sin of missing these acts persists despite apostasy. On the other hand, acts of worship that were not obligatory (like missed prayers during the apostasy period) are not required because, according to the Hanafi school, disbelievers (including apostates) are not addressed by the divine commands (khitab al-kufar). Therefore, the apostate does not make up missed prayers or fasts from the period of apostasy itself. The proof is rational: the address of the Shari'a does not apply to a disbeliever, so no obligation arises during apostasy.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam by word, deed, or belief.
وقف (waqf): An endowment of property for pious purposes or for family then charity.
خطاب الكفار بالشرائع (khitab al-kuffar bi al-shara'i'): The question of whether disbelievers are addressed by the divine commands of Shari'a.
قضاء (qada'): Making up missed obligatory acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because apostasy nullifies all past good deeds.
B) Because disbelievers are not addressed by the commands of Shari'a.
C) Because the apostate was too sinful to be accountable.
D) Because prayers are only obligatory on Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy nullifies current acts of piety (like waqf) but does not erase obligations incurred before apostasy; however, no new obligations arise during apostasy due to the Hanafi principle that disbelievers are not addressed by Shari'a.

Ruling on Killing a Male Apostate
Ruling on liability and dislike for killing a male apostate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a male apostate, identify the circumstances under which it is disliked, and explain why the killer is not liable.

Core Idea
Killing a male apostate is legally permissible, but it is disliked to do so before offering him Islam.

The Hanafi school holds that the blood of a male apostate is lawful because disbelief permits killing. However, the school also teaches that it is better to first invite him back to Islam, making his killing before that invitation disliked. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the exception of liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from the matn.
The base text states: 'The killer is not liable' (لا يضمن قاتله). This means that if a male apostate is killed, there is no blood money or qisas upon the killer.
This applies whether the killer is the Imam or anyone else, but if it is someone else, the Imam may discipline him.
2
Understand the disliked nature of killing before dawah.
The commentary explains that it is 'makruh tanzih' (disliked, not sinful) to kill the apostate before presenting Islam to him, because his return is hoped for. If presenting Islam is considered obligatory, the dislike becomes 'makruh tahrimi' (prohibitive).
This difference depends on whether the ijtihad treats the dawah as obligatory or recommend.
3
Analyze the proof for non-liability.
The reason given is 'because disbelief permits killing' (لأن الكفر مبيح للقتل). The apostate's disbelief makes his blood unprotected, similar to a combatant in war.
Thus, the killer incurs no financial or corporal penalty.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on the obligation of dawah.
Some Hanafi scholars (like those cited in Fath al-Qadir) hold that presenting Islam to the apostate before killing is wajib; others say it is mustahab. This affects whether the dislike is tanzihi or tahrimi.
This difference reflects varying weight given to the hadith of calling to Islam before fighting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير / باب أحكام المرتدين لا يضمن قاتله ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى تسلم. قوله: (وكره قتله قبله) أي قبل عرض الإسلام لأن إسلامه مرجو. قال في الهداية: ومعنى الكراهة هنا ترك المستحب اهـ. يعني فهي كراهة تنزيه وهو مبني على القول باستحباب العرض، وأما من قال بوجوبه فهي كراهة تحريم كما في فتح القدير. أطلقه فشمل قتل الإمام وغيره لكن إن قتله غيره أو قطع عضواً منه بغير إذن الإمام أدبه الإمام كما في شرح الطحاوي. قوله: (ولم يضمن قاتله لأن الكفر مبيح للقتل وكل جناية على المرتد فهي هدر). قوله: (ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى تسلم) النهي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن قتل النساء ولأن الأصل تأخير الأجزية إلى دار الآخرة إذ تعجيلها يخل بمعنى الابتلاء، وإنما عدل عنه دفعاً لشر ناجز وهو الحراب ولا يتوجه ذلك من النساء لعدم صلاحية البنية بخلاف الرجال فصارت كالمرتدة الأصلية. أطلقها فشمل الحرة والأمة. ويستثنى منه المرتدة بالسحر لما في المحيط. والساحرة تقتل إذا كانت تعتقد أنها هي الخالقة لذلك لتصير مرتدة وإن كانت المرتدة لا تقتل لما جاء في أن عمر رضي الله عنه كتب إلى عماله أن اقتلوا الساحر والساحرة. وذكر في المنتقى من الأثر أن الساحرة لا تقتل ولكنها تحبس وتضرب كالمرتدة والأول أصح لأن ضرر كفرها وهو سحرها يتعدى إلى الحي المعصوم بفوات حياته فتقتل كالرجل. اهـ. وفي التتارخانية: الخنثى المشكل إذا ارتد لم يقتل ويحبس ويجبر على الإسلام. اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم قاتلها قال في فتح القدير: ولو قتلها قاتل لا شيء عليه حرة كانت أو أمة ذكره في المبسوط اهـ. وفي التتارخانية معزياً إلى العتابية وفي الأمة يضم لمولاها اهـ. وفي الولوالجية: وإن قتلها قاتل لم يضمن شيئاً لأن قيمة الدم بالإسلام وقد زال ويؤدب على ذلك لارتكابه ما لا يحل اهـ. وظاهر كلامه أنه لا فرق بين الحرة والأمة في عدم الضمان فإنه قال أولاً: ومن قتل حرة مرتدة لم يضمن ثم قال: وكذا الأمة وأطلق في حبسها فشمل الأمة لكن الأمة تدفع إلى مولاها فيجعل حبسها بيت السيد، سواء طلب هو ذلك أم لا في الصحيح، ويتولى هو جبرها جمعاً بين حق الله وحق السيد في الاستخدام فإنه لا منافاة بخلاف العبد المرتد لأنه لا فائدة في دفعه إليه لأنه يقتل. ويستثنى من خدمته لها وطؤها فقد صرح الأسبيجابي بأنه لا يطؤها، وقدمنا عن الولوالجي ما يفيده. وأفاد بقوله «تحبس» أنها لا تسترق في دار الإسلام وقدمنا فيه رواية في باب نكاح الكافر مع بقية أحكام ردتها فارجع إليه. ولم يذكر المصنف أنها تضرب لأنه لم يذكر في الجامع الكبير ولا في ظاهر الرواية وقد نقل الشارحون في باب نكاح الكافر أنها إذا ارتدت تضرب خمسة وسبعين وهو اختيار لقول أبي يوسف في نهاية التعزير الفضلاء وعليه فالظاهر أن في عبارة المؤلف قلباً فإن المجوسي جاحد للباري تعالى بخلاف الوثني فإن عبدة الأوثان هم المشركون قوله فصارت كالمرتدة (الأصلية كذا في النسخ ولعله «الكافرة»). ثم استمر الكلام في بيان أحكام الضرب: وذكر في فتح القدير هنا: ويروى عن أبي حنيفة أنها تضرب في كل يوم وقدرها بعضهم بثلاثة، وعن الحسن تضرب في كل يوم تسعة وثلاثين سوطاً إلى أن تموت أو تسلم. ولم يخصه بحرة ولا أمة وهذا قتل لأن موالاة الضرب تفضي إليه. اهـ. وأطلق في حبسها فشمل ما إذا لحقت بدار الحرب ثم سبيت واسترقت فإنها تجبر على الإسلام بالضرب والحبس ولا تقتل كما صرح به في البدائع، ولا يكون استرقاقها مسقطاً عنها الجبر على الإسلام كما لو ارتدت الأمة ابتداء فإنها تجبر على الإسلام. وشمل ما إذا كانت صغيرة عاقلة لما في المحيط من باب ما يجب للمطلقة قبل الدخول ما يجب جزاء على الردة: يجوز أن تؤاخذ الصغيرة به ألا ترى أنها تحبس على الردة كما تحبس الكبيرة والحبس جزاء الردة اهـ. جميع
Book of Siyar / Chapter on Rulings of Apostates. The killer is not liable, and the female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim. His statement: (And it is disliked to kill him before that) i.e., before presenting Islam because his becoming Muslim is hoped for. Al-Hidayah said: The meaning of dislike here is leaving the preferred. So it is tanzihi dislike, based on the view that presenting is recommended. As for whoever said it is obligatory, it is tahrimi dislike as in Fath al-Qadir. He made it general, so it includes killing by the Imam or other, but if someone else kills him or cuts a limb without the Imam's permission, the Imam disciplines him as in Sharh al-Tahawi. His statement: (And the killer is not liable because disbelief permits killing, and every injury against the apostate is without compensation.) His statement: (And the female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim) due to the Prophet's prohibition of killing women, and because the original principle is to delay punishment to the Hereafter, since hastening it contradicts the meaning of trial. Rather, it was departed from to repel immediate evil, which is combat, and that does not apply to women due to lack of physical suitability, unlike men. So she becomes like the original female apostate. He made it general, so it includes free women and slave women. Excepted from this is the apostate by sorcery, as in al-Muhit. The sorceress is killed if she believes she is the creator of that, thus becoming an apostate, even though the female apostate is not killed, because of what came that Umar wrote to his governors to kill the male and female sorcerer. Mentioned in al-Muntaqa min al-Athar that the sorceress is not killed but imprisoned and beaten like the female apostate, and the first is more correct because the harm of her disbelief, i.e., her sorcery, extends to the protected life by causing loss of life, so she is killed like a man. End quote. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: The ambiguous hermaphrodite, if he apostatizes, is not killed but imprisoned and forced to Islam. End quote. The author did not mention the ruling on her killer. It is said in Fath al-Qadir: If a killer kills her, nothing is upon him, whether free or slave, as mentioned in al-Mabsut. End quote. In al-Tatarkhaniyya, citing al-Atabiyya: and regarding the slave woman, she is referred to her master. End quote. In al-Walwalijiyya: If a killer kills her, he does not guarantee anything because the value of blood is by Islam and it has ceased, and he is disciplined for committing what is not permissible. End quote. The apparent meaning of his words is that there is no difference between free and slave in lack of liability, for he said first: Whoever kills a free female apostate does not guarantee, then said: Likewise the slave. And he made it general in her imprisonment, so it includes the slave woman, but the slave woman is given to her master, and her imprisonment is made in the master's house, whether he asks for that or not according to the sound view, and he undertakes to force her, combining the right of Allah and the right of the master to service, for there is no contradiction, unlike the male slave apostate because there is no benefit in handing him over since he is killed. Excepted from his service to her is intercourse with her, for al-Asbijabi explicitly stated that he does not have intercourse with her, and we have previously mentioned from al-Walwaliji what indicates that. And he indicated by his saying 'imprisoned' that she is not enslaved in the Abode of Islam, and we have previously mentioned a narration in the chapter on marriage of the disbeliever with the rest of the rulings on her apostasy, so refer to it. The author did not mention that she is beaten because he did not mention it in al-Jami' al-Kabir nor in Zahir al-Riwaya, but the commentators have transmitted in the chapter on marriage of the disbeliever that if she apostatizes, she is beaten seventy-five lashes, and that is the choice of Abu Yusuf in the ultimate ta'zir. The virtuous ones said: Based on this, it appears that there is an inversion in the author's expression, for the Magian is a denier of the Exalted Creator unlike the idolater, for the idolaters are polytheists. His saying: 'so she becomes like the original female apostate' (in the copies as such, and perhaps it is 'al-kafira'). Then the speech continued in explaining the rulings of beating: It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir here: It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that she is beaten every day, and some estimated it as three, and from al-Hasan that she is beaten every day thirty-nine lashes until she dies or becomes Muslim. He did not specify it to free or slave, and this is killing because continuous beating leads to it. End quote. And he made it general in her imprisonment, so it includes if she joined Dar al-Harb and then was captured and enslaved, for she is forced to Islam by beating and imprisonment and is not killed, as stated in al-Bada'i, and her enslavement does not remove the compulsion to Islam, just as if a slave woman apostatized initially, she is forced to Islam. And it includes if she was a minor with intellect, as in al-Muhit from the chapter on what is obligatory for the divorced woman before consummation: that which is obligatory as a penalty for apostasy: it is permissible to hold the minor accountable for it; do you not see that she is imprisoned for apostasy as the adult is imprisoned? And imprisonment is the penalty for apostasy. End quote. All.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the first two rulings on apostates: the male apostate's killing and the female apostate's imprisonment. The author begins by stating the matn: the killer of a male apostate is not liable for compensation, and the female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she repents. The commentary then explains that it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to kill the male apostate before presenting Islam to him, because his return is hoped for; the dislike is actually that of leaving a superior act. If someone other than the Imam kills the apostate preemptively, the Imam may discipline him but no blood-money is due. The proof for the male apostate's killing is that disbelief makes his blood lawful. For the female apostate, the proof is the Prophet's prohibition of killing women and the rationale that punishment is deferred to the Hereafter; the immediate execution is reserved for armed combatants, which women are not suited for. Exceptions are discussed: a sorceress whose disbelief causes harm by killing may be killed, and a hermaphrodite is imprisoned. The killer of a female apostate is also not liable, and the slave woman's imprisonment is in her master's house. The passage then addresses the beating (ta'zir) of the female apostate: though not in Zahir al-Riwaya, later scholars transmit that she is beaten; Abu Yusuf set the maximum at 75 lashes, while Abu Hanifa reportedly allowed daily beating in discretion. The text concludes that imprisonment applies even if she is captured from Dar al-Harb or is a minor.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam by word or deed.
كراهة تنزيه (karāhat tanzīh): A disliked act that is not sinful, but it is better to avoid.
تعزير (ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment for sins not having a fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on killing a male apostate before presenting Islam to him?
A) It is haram and the killer is liable for blood money.
B) It is mubah but disliked (makruh tanzih).
C) It is wajib to kill immediately without delay.
D) It is permissible only if the killer is the Imam.

Key Takeaway
A male apostate's blood is lawful; killing him incurs no liability, but it is disliked to do so before inviting him back to Islam.

intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Imprisoning a Female Apostate
Ruling on imprisonment of female apostate and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a female apostate, identify the exception of a sorceress, and explain the proof for not killing her.

Core Idea
A female apostate is never killed but imprisoned until she repents; the Prophet's prohibition of killing women is the key proof.

Unlike the male apostate, the female apostate is not executed but imprisoned indefinitely until she returns to Islam. This ruling is based on the Prophetic prohibition of killing women and the principle that women are not suited for combat. However, an exception exists for a sorceress whose harm extends to killing. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the intra-Hanafi differences on corporal punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from the matn.
The base text states: 'The female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim' (ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى تسلم).
This applies to free women and slave women, but the slave woman's imprisonment is in her master's house.
2
Understand the proof from the Sunnah and rationale.
The commentary cites the Prophet's prohibition of killing women (النهي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن قتل النساء) and the rationale that punishment is deferred to the Hereafter; immediate execution is only for armed combatants, which women are not suited for.
Thus, the female apostate is treated like the original disbelieving woman who is not killed.
3
Note the exception: the sorceress.
A female apostate who practices sorcery and believes herself the creator may be killed, because her harm extends to taking lives. This is based on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab ordering the execution of sorcerers.
The text notes a differing view that the sorceress is only imprisoned and beaten, but the preferred view is execution.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference on beating (ta'zir).
Although the matn does not mention beating, later commentaries transmit that the female apostate is beaten as ta'zir. Abu Hanifa reportedly allowed daily beating in the judge's discretion; Abu Yusuf set the maximum at 75 lashes; Hasan al-Basri said 39 lashes daily.
The relied-upon position leaves the number to the judge's ijtihad, but she is never killed through beating.

كتاب السير / باب أحكام المرتدين لا يضمن قاتله ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى تسلم. قوله: (وكره قتله قبله) أي قبل عرض الإسلام لأن إسلامه مرجو. قال في الهداية: ومعنى الكراهة هنا ترك المستحب اهـ. يعني فهي كراهة تنزيه وهو مبني على القول باستحباب العرض، وأما من قال بوجوبه فهي كراهة تحريم كما في فتح القدير. أطلقه فشمل قتل الإمام وغيره لكن إن قتله غيره أو قطع عضواً منه بغير إذن الإمام أدبه الإمام كما في الدخول ما يجب جزاء على الردة: يجوز أن تؤاخذ الصغيرة به ألا ترى أنها تحبس على الردة كما تحبس الكبيرة والحبس جزاء الردة اهـ. جميع

And he made it general in her imprisonment, so it includes if she joined Dar al-Harb and then was captured and enslaved, for she is forced to Islam by beating and imprisonment and is not killed, as stated in al-Bada'i, and her enslavement does not remove the compulsion to Islam, just as if a slave woman apostatized initially, she is forced to Islam. And it includes if she was a minor with intellect, as in al-Muhit from the chapter on what is obligatory for the divorced woman before consummation: that which is obligatory as a penalty for apostasy: it is permissible to hold the minor accountable for it; do you not see that she is imprisoned for apostasy as the adult is imprisoned? And imprisonment is the penalty for apostasy. End quote. All.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the first two rulings on apostates: the male apostate's killing and the female apostate's imprisonment. The author begins by stating the matn: the killer of a male apostate is not liable for compensation, and the female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she repents. The commentary then explains that it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to kill the male apostate before presenting Islam to him, because his return is hoped for; the dislike is actually that of leaving a superior act. If someone other than the Imam kills the apostate preemptively, the Imam may discipline him but no blood-money is due. The proof for the male apostate's killing is that disbelief makes his blood lawful. For the female apostate, the proof is the Prophet's prohibition of killing women and the rationale that punishment is deferred to the Hereafter; the immediate execution is reserved for armed combatants, which women are not suited for. Exceptions are discussed: a sorceress whose disbelief causes harm by killing may be killed, and a hermaphrodite is imprisoned. The killer of a female apostate is also not liable, and the slave woman's imprisonment is in her master's house. The passage then addresses the beating (ta'zir) of the female apostate: though not in Zahir al-Riwaya, later scholars transmit that she is beaten; Abu Yusuf set the maximum at 75 lashes, while Abu Hanifa reportedly allowed daily beating in discretion. The text concludes that imprisonment applies even if she is captured from Dar al-Harb or is a minor.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam by word or deed.
كراهة تنزيه (karāhat tanzīh): A disliked act that is not sinful, but it is better to avoid.
تعزير (ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment for sins not having a fixed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following statements is correct about a female apostate?
A) She is killed like a male apostate.
B) She is imprisoned until she repents, and if she is a sorceress, she is killed.
C) She is immediately enslaved and sold.
D) She is released after a fixed term of imprisonment.

Key Takeaway
A female apostate is never killed but imprisoned until she repents; the hadith prohibiting the killing of women is the primary proof, with an exception only for the sorceress.

Effects of the Apostate Joining Dar al-Harb
Ruling on freeing of mudabbars and umm walad, and debt due upon apostate's joining dar al-harb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal effects of an apostate (murtadd) joining dar al-harb (lahaq) according to the Hanafi school and explain why the qadi's judgment is required.

Core Idea
The apostate who joins dar al-harb is treated as dead; his mudabbars and umm walad become free, and debts become due—but only after the qadi's judgment.

In this lesson, we examine a detailed passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq on the consequences of an apostate (murtadd) joining enemy territory (dar al-harb). The Hanafi school treats this act as equivalent to death in many respects, but with important procedural requirements. We will explore the freeing of mudabbars and umm walad, the immediate due of debts, and the necessity of a qadi's judgment. We will also address a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of inheritance.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for mudabbars and umm walad
Identify the legal effect: upon the qadi's judgment of lahaq, the apostate's mudabbars and umm walad become free, and his debts become due.
This is like actual death.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas: the apostate who joins dar al-harb is treated as dead because the authority of Islamic law over him ceases, just as a dead person is no longer subject to obligations.
This is qiyas jaliy.
3
Explain the need for qadi's judgment
The legal effects do not occur automatically; they require the qadi's judgment (qada') because of the possibility that the apostate may return to Islam.
The judgment establishes the legal death.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on inheritance timing
Abu Yusuf considers the time of qadi's judgment for determining heirs; Muhammad considers the time of actual lahaq. The relied-upon view is Muhammad's.
The practical consequence: if an heir dies between lahaq and judgment, different heirs inherit.
5
Apply the ruling to related cases
Consider the female apostate: she does not become fay' because she is not a combatant. Also the mukatab: his earnings during apostasy go to his master, not the state.
This shows the limits of the analogy.

قال شاء الله تعالى. وقدمنا أن الكلام إنما هو في الحر وفي الجوهرة: إن ما اكتسبه المكاتب في حال ردته لا يكون فيئاً وإنما يكون لمولاه لتعلق حقه به. وقيد بالمرتد لأن المرتدة كسبها لورثتها لأنه لا حراب منها فلم يوجد سبب الفيء بخلاف المرتد عند أبي حنيفة، ويرثها زوجها المسلم إن ارتدت وهي مريضة لقصدها إبطال حقه، وإن كانت صحيحة لا يرثها لأنها لا تقتل فلم يتعلق حقه بمالها بالردة بخلاف المرتد. والحاصل أن زوجة المرتد ترث منه مطلقاً وزوج المرتدة لا يرثها إلا إذا ارتدت مريضة

مدبريها وحلول دين عليها. ولم يذكر قسمة ماله بين ورثته لظهوره ولما سيشير إليه عند قوله فما وجده في يد وارثه. ولم يذكر حكم مكاتبه وحكمه كما في البدائع أنه يؤدى إلى الورثة فيعتق وإذا عتق فولاؤه للمرتد لأنه المعتق. وفي المجتبى: القضاء باللحاق ليس بشرط وإنما يشترط قضاؤه بشيء من أحكام الموتى. وعامتهم على أنه يشترط القضاء باللحاق سابقاً على قضائه بهذه الأحكام وإليه أشار محمد في كثير من المواضع. وفي فتح له فقال أبو يوسف: يقضي به كان وارثاً وقت القضاء بلحاقه لأنه حينئذ يصير موتاً. وقال محمد: يعتبر وقت لحاقه لأنه السبب. كذا في المجتبى. وفي التتارخانية: وإذا ارتد الأب مع بعض أولاده ولحقوا بدار الحرب ارتد ولحق معه إذا مات مرتداً، فإن لحق أحد من أولاده مسلماً معه فإنه يرث كسب إسلامه فقط.
Book of Siyar/Chapter on Rulings of Apostates. His mudabbars and umm walad become free, his debt becomes due, and his transactions (sale, manumission, gift) are suspended; if he returns to Islam, they are effective, and if he dies, they are void. He (the commentator) said: 'By the will of Allah.' And we have previously stated that the discussion is only concerning the free person... and in al-Jawharah: what the mukatab earns during his apostasy is not fay' but belongs to his master due to his right being attached to it. And it is restricted to the apostate because the female apostate's earnings are for her heirs since there is no harb from her, so the cause of fay' does not exist unlike the apostate according to Abu Hanifah... His statement: 'And if judgment is passed on his joining (dar al-harb), his mudabbars and umm walad become free and his debt becomes due' because by joining he becomes one of the people of war, and they are dead with respect to Islamic rulings due to the cessation of the authority of compulsion... Except that his joining is not established except by the qadi's judgment due to the possibility of his returning to us... And when his death is established, the rulings related to it are established: the freeing of the mudabbar and umm walad, and the expiry of the term (for debt) as in actual death...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the rulings of an apostate who has joined dar al-harb. The passage begins by stating the central ruling: when the apostate joins dar al-harb, his mudabbars (slaves promised freedom upon his death) and his umm walad (slave mother of his child) become free, and any debts he owes become immediately due. These effects are likened to actual death because the apostate, by joining the enemy, is considered legally dead in Islamic law—the authority to compel him ceases. However, this legal death is not automatic; it requires the qadi's judgment (qada' bil-lahaq) because there is still a possibility that the apostate may return. The author then clarifies that this ruling applies only to the free apostate, not the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission). A distinction is also made between the male and female apostate: the female apostate's earnings go to her heirs because she is not considered a combatant (la harba minha), and her Muslim husband inherits from her only if she apostatized while ill (to prevent her from depriving him). The passage then delves into a dispute between the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the timing of inheritance: Abu Yusuf considers the time of the qadi's judgment on lahaq, while Muhammad considers the time of actual lahaq. The commentator discusses the necessity of the qadi's judgment and notes that some scholars hold that judgment on lahaq must precede the specific rulings (like freeing of mudabbars), while others hold that a judgment on the specific effect suffices. The passage also touches on the inheritance of the apostate's property and the status of his earnings during apostasy, distinguishing between earnings from Islam (which go to Muslim heirs) and earnings from apostasy (which become fay' for the Muslims). Throughout, the author follows the Hanafi school, presenting the positions of Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Key Terms
لحاق (lahaq): The act of an apostate joining dar al-harb (enemy territory) physically or constructively.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whom the master has promised freedom upon the master's death (by saying 'you are free after my death').
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, where the child is recognized as free and legitimate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal effect of an apostate (murtadd) joining dar al-harb (lahaq) regarding his mudabbars and umm walad?
A) They become free immediately upon his apostasy.
B) They become free only after the qadi's judgment of lahaq, but the umm walad is freed from the entire estate and mudabbar from one-third.
C) They do not become free; the apostate retains ownership.
D) They become free only if the apostate dies in dar al-harb.

Key Takeaway
The legal effects of the apostate joining dar al-harb (lahaq) mirror those of death, but only upon the qadi's judgment, reflecting the Hanafi's blend of substantive and procedural law.

Child Born to an Apostate's Slave Woman: Inheritance and Religion
Ruling on the child's religion and inheritance from an apostate father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the child's religion and inheritance when the mother is Christian or Muslim, and apply the six-month gestation rule.

Core Idea
The child's inheritance and religion follow the best of the parents, but uncertainty of conception makes the child an apostate.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a nuanced ruling concerning a child born to an apostate's slave woman. The outcome hinges on two factors: the religion of the mother and the timing of birth relative to the father's apostasy. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi principle that the child's religion follows the best of the parents, but also that uncertainty in conception can lead to the child being deemed an apostate and thus incapable of inheriting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between the mother being Christian (or Kitabi) and the mother being Muslim. This is the primary factor determining the child's religion.
The term 'Christian' includes all Kitabi (People of the Book).
2
Apply the six-month rule
When the mother is non-Muslim, the time of birth relative to apostasy is crucial. If the child is born less than six months after apostasy, there is certainty of conception before apostasy, so the child is Muslim. If six months or more, uncertainty exists, and the child is deemed an apostate.
The six-month period is the minimum pregnancy term; it is used to establish certainty.
3
Determine inheritance consequence
A Muslim child can inherit from the apostate father; an apostate child cannot. Apostates do not inherit from anyone, and the apostate father cannot inherit from them either.
The apostate's property is treated as fay’ for the public treasury.
4
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The child's religion follows the best of the parents. When the mother is Muslim, she is better in religion, so the child is Muslim. When the mother is non-Muslim, the father (though apostate) is considered closer to Islam because he is compelled to return, so the child follows him as an apostate—unless certainty of conception before apostasy proves otherwise.
This is an application of istihsan, balancing the principle of following the best religion with the certainty of conception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير / باب أحكام المرتدين
ولدت أمة له نصرانية لستة أشهر منذ ارتد فادعاه فهي أم ولده وهو ابنه حر ولا يرثه حربي [؟] الخلافة بل لكونه مال كما قدمناه فصار لبيت المال فلا يسترده كما أن الحربي الحقيقي لا يسترد ماله بعد إسلامه. وقيد بقوله بعد الحكم بلحاقه لأنه لو عاد مسلماً قبله فحكمه كما إذا لم يرتد فلا يعتق مدبره وأم ولده ولا تحل ديونه وله إبطال ما تصرف فيه الوارث لكونه فضولياً.
قوله : (ولو ولدت أمة له نصرانية لستة أشهر منذ ارتد فادعاه فهي أم ولده وهو ابنه حر ولا يرثه ولو مسلمة ورثه الابن إن مات على الردة أو لحق بدار الحرب) أما صحة الاستيلاد فلما قدمنا أنه لا يفتقر إلى حقيقة الملك، وأما الإرث فلأن الأم إذا كانت نصرانية فالولد تبع له لقربه إلى الإسلام للجبر عليه فصار في حكم المرتد والمرتد لا يرث أحداً، ولم يجعل مسلماً تبعاً للدار لأنها عند عدم الأبوين فقط، أما إذا كانت مسلمة فالولد مسلم تبعاً لها لأنها خيرهما ديناً، والمسلم يرث المرتد . أراد بالنصرانية الكتابية ولو يهودية، والتقييد بالستة لنفي الأقل فإنها إذا جاءت به لأقل منها فالولد يرث من أبيه المرتد للتيقن بوجوده في البطن قبل الردة فيكون مسلماً تبعاً للأب بخلافه للستة لعدم التيقن كما في النهاية لا لنفي الأكثر ولذا عبر في الهداية بالأكثر . زاد فتح القدير ولو إلى عشر سنين
A female slave belonging to him, who is Christian, gives birth six months after he apostatized, and he claims the child. Then she is an umm walad, and the child is his son, free, and does not inherit from him [the apostate] as a harbi? The caliphate but because it is property as we have mentioned, so it becomes for the public treasury and he cannot reclaim it just as a real harbi cannot reclaim his property after his Islam. And he qualified it by his saying 'after the adjudication of his joining [dar al-harb]' because if he returned Muslim before it, his ruling is as if he did not apostatize: his mudabbar and umm walad are not manumitted, his debts are not dissolved, and he has the right to nullify what the heir disposed of because the heir is a usurper. His saying: (And if a female slave belonging to him, Christian, gives birth six months since his apostasy, and he claims it, then she is an umm walad and he is his son, free, and he does not inherit from him; and if [the mother] is Muslim, the son inherits from him if he dies in apostasy or joins dar al-harb.) As for the validity of istilad, it is because we have stated that it does not require actual ownership. As for inheritance, because if the mother is Christian, the child follows him [the father] due to his closeness to Islam because he is compelled to it, so the child is in the ruling of an apostate, and an apostate does not inherit from anyone. And he is not made a Muslim following the dar, because that is only in the absence of parents. But if she is Muslim, the child is Muslim following her because she is the better of the two in religion, and a Muslim inherits from an apostate. He meant by 'Christian' the Kitabi, even if Jewish. And the restriction to six months is to negate less than that, because if she brings him at less than that, the child inherits from his apostate father because of certainty of his existence in the womb before apostasy, so he is Muslim following the father, unlike six months because of lack of certainty, as in an-Nihayah; it is not to negate more, so he expressed in al-Hidayah with 'the most'. Fath al-Qadir added: even up to ten years.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the status of a child born to an apostate's slave woman. The author explains two scenarios: if the mother is Christian (or Jewish), the child follows the father in being considered an apostate and thus cannot inherit from the apostate (nor can the apostate inherit from the child). However, if the mother is Muslim, the child is Muslim and can inherit from the apostate father. The key underlying principle is that the child's religion follows the best of the parents, but when the mother is non-Muslim and the father is apostate, the child is deemed an apostate because he is closer to Islam due to his father's obligation to return to Islam. The six-month gestation period is crucial: if the child is born less than six months after apostasy, it is certain that he was conceived before apostasy and thus is Muslim; if six months or more, it is uncertain, so he is deemed apostate. The ruling demonstrates the Hanafi approach of combining istihsan (juristic preference) with strict analogy.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears her master's child and becomes free upon his death.
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam and joins dar al-harb or is adjudged as such.
استيلاد (istilad): The legal recognition of a slave woman as the mother of the master's child, giving her umm walad status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The child does not inherit because he is considered an apostate.
C) The child inherits if he is Muslim.
D) The child inherits only if the mother is Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The child's inheritance from an apostate father depends on the mother's religion and the certainty of conception before apostasy, following the principle that the child's religion is the best of the parents.

Kitabah by Heir of Apostate: Return to Islam and Transfer of Rights
Ruling on kitabah by heir and effect of apostate's return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a kitabah contract executed by an apostate's heir and determine when the contract and wala' transfer to the returning apostate.

Core Idea
The heir's kitabah is valid; upon the apostate's return, the contract and wala' revert to him.

In this ruling, we examine a scenario where an apostate's son, after the judge's ruling, enters into a kitabah contract with his father's slave. If the apostate returns to Islam, the crucial question is: who owns the kitabah contract and the wala'? The Hanafi school has an established position, but there is an internal difference regarding the timing of the return. We will unpack the ruling, its reasoning, and the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The core scenario: an apostate joins dar al-harb; the judge rules his slave belongs to his son (the heir); the son makes a kitabah contract with the slave; then the apostate returns as a Muslim before the son receives the kitabah compensation.
The payment condition is critical: if the son already received payment, the ruling changes.
2
Understand the Heir's Role
The heir acts as a deputy (al-khalaf) for the apostate. The kitabah contract issued by the heir is valid because it stems from a valid guardianship (the judge's ruling). The rights of the contract belong to the original owner (the apostate).
3
Apply the Condition of Compensation
The ruling applies only if the son has not yet received the kitabah compensation. If he received it, the slave is freed by the son and wala' stays with the son, just as if the son had manumitted the slave directly.
The text uses the letter fa (ف) to indicate immediate sequence: 'faja'a musliman' means coming before payment.
4
Distinguish Between Absolute and Restricted Views
The apparent (zahir) of the riwaya is absolute: the ruling applies regardless of when the apostate returns (before or after the judge's ruling). Abu al-Layth restricted it to return after the judge's ruling. The relied-upon view is the absolute one.
This ikhtilaf does not change the outcome in the given scenario (return after judge's ruling) but would affect a scenario where return happens before the ruling.
5
Contrast with Tadbir
The ruling is specific to kitabah. If the son had made a tadbir (postponed emancipation) instead, the wala' would not transfer to the father upon return.
This highlights the unique nature of kitabah as a binding contract that transfers rights.
