Rights of Congregants in a Crowded Mosque
First part of passage covering crowding and mosque division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rights of a worshiper in a crowded mosque and apply the rules for dividing or merging mosques.

Core Idea
A worshiper may displace a seated person even engaged in worship; the community may divide a mosque into separate prayer areas.

This part of the passage addresses practical congregational issues: what happens when the mosque is full, and how the community can manage space. It also covers the permissibility of dividing one mosque into two or merging two into one for congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling when the mosque is crowded
The text states that a worshiper may displace a sitting person from his place to pray, even if that person is engaged in dhikr, lesson, Quran recitation, or i'tikaf.
2
Understand community authority over entrance
The people of the neighborhood may prevent outsiders from entering when the mosque is crowded.
3
Distinguish dividing vs. merging mosques
Dividing a mosque into two with separate imams and one mu'adhdhin is permissible, and it is better each group has its own mu'adhdhin. Merging two mosques into one is only allowed for congregational prayer, not for teaching or reminders because mosques are built for prayer.
4
Recognize the principle behind the rulings
The underlying principle is that mosques are dedicated to prayer; other activities are secondary and must not conflict with the primary purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له متاع في المسجد يخاف عليه فإنه يتيمم ويدخل في الصلاة، وإذا ضاق المسجد كان للمصلي أن يزعج القاعد من موضعه ليصلي فيه وإن كان مشتغلاً بالذكر أو الدرس أو قراءة القرآن أو الاعتكاف وكذا لأهل المحلة أن يمنعوا من ليس منهم عن فيه إذا ضاق بهم المسجد. أهل المحلة قسموا المسجد وضربوا فيه حائطاً ولكل منهم إمام على حدة ومؤذنهم واحد لا بأس به، والأولى أن يكون لكل طائفة مؤذن كما يجوز لأهل المحلة أن يجعلوا المسجد الواحد مسجدين فلهم أن يجعلوا المسجدين واحداً لإقامة الجماعة أما للتذكير أو للتدريس فلا لأنه ما بنى له وإن جاز فيه. وفي شرح الآثار أن البيع وخصف النعل وإنشاد الشعر مما كان لا هذا غير مكروه، وما يعمه منه أو يغلبه فمكروه. ويجوز الدرس في المسجد وإن كان فيه استعمال اللبود والبواري المسبلة لأجل المسجد، لو علم الصبيان القرآن في المسجد لا يجوز ويأثم، وكذا التأديب فيه أي لا يجوز التأديب فيه إذا كان بأجر، وينبغي أن يجوز بغير أجر، وأما الصبيان فقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «جنبوا مساجدكم صبيانكم ومجانينكم وكذا لا يجوز التعليم في دكان في فناء المسجد؛ هذا عند أبي حنيفة . وعندهما يجوز إذا لم يضر بالعامة . أصابه البرد الشديد في الطريق فدخل مسجداً فيه خشب الغير ولو لم يوقد ناراً يهلك فخشب المسجد في الإيقاد أولى من غيره، يجوز إدخال الحبوب وأثاث البيت في المسجد للخوف في الفتنة العامة .اهـ وفيها من الوقف : اتخذا مسجداً على أنه بالخيار جاز المسجد والشرط باطل جعل وسط داره مسجداً وأذن للناس في الدخول يعم المسجد من وقد خالف فيه قاضيخان كما مر فتدبر اهـ. ويؤيده قول الإسعاف لأنه لا بد من التأبيد والتوقيت
If he has property in the mosque that he fears for, he may perform tayammum and enter the prayer. And if the mosque is crowded, the worshiper may displace the sitting person from his place to pray, even if he is engaged in dhikr, lesson, Quran recitation, or i'tikaf. Similarly, the people of the neighborhood may prevent those who are not from among them from entering when the mosque is crowded. The people of the neighborhood divided the mosque and built a wall in it, each having a separate imam and a single mu'adhdhin; there is nothing wrong with it, and it is better that each group has its own mu'adhdhin. And it is permissible for the people of the neighborhood to make one mosque into two mosques, and likewise to make two mosques into one for the purpose of congregational prayer, but not for the purpose of reminding or teaching, because it was not built for that, even if it is permissible within it. In Sharh al-Athar: Buying, patching sandals, and reciting poetry (was not disliked), but that which distracts or overcomes is disliked. And teaching a lesson in the mosque is permissible, even if it involves using carpets and mats dedicated for the mosque. Teaching the Quran to children in the mosque is not permissible and is sinful, similarly disciplining (children) in it is not permissible if it is for pay, but it should be permissible without pay. As for children, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Keep your children and madmen away from your mosques.' Similarly, teaching in a shop in the courtyard of the mosque is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two disciples it is permissible if it does not harm the public. If someone is affected by severe cold on the road and enters a mosque containing wood belonging to others, and if he does not light a fire he will perish, then the wood of the mosque is more appropriate for lighting than other wood. It is permissible to bring in grains and household furniture into the mosque due to fear of public strife. End. And in it from the chapter on waqf: Two people took a place as a mosque on the condition that they have an option; the mosque is valid and the condition is void. If someone made the center of his house a mosque and gave permission for people to enter, does it apply to all? Qadikhan disagreed as has passed, so ponder. End. And it is supported by the statement of al-Is'af because it requires perpetuity, and temporality (invalidates).
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage concludes with a variety of rulings. When the mosque is crowded, a worshiper has the right to ask a sitting person to move even if that person is engaged in worship. However, per Hanafi view, one cannot claim a specific spot as his own. The community may divide a mosque into two sections with separate imams but one mu'adhdhin, and it is better each has its own mu'adhdhin. Merging two mosques is only allowed for congregational prayer, not for teaching or reminders. Teaching children the Quran for pay in the mosque is prohibited and sinful, but without pay it may be allowed; the hadith 'Keep your children and madmen away from your mosques' is cited. Teaching in a shop in the mosque courtyard is not allowed according to Abu Hanifa, but permissible according to the two disciples if no harm to public. If a person is in danger of freezing, he may use wood belonging to the mosque (even if waqf) because preservation of life takes precedence. It is permissible to store grain and furniture in the mosque due to civil strife. Finally, if someone makes a mosque with a condition that they have the option to revoke, the mosque is valid but the condition is void because waqf requires perpetuity. Qadikhan has a differing opinion on whether permission to enter applies to all, but the author supports the view that perpetuity is necessary.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-I'tikaf): Seclusion in the mosque for worship, often for a set period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, merging two mosques into one is permissible for which purpose?
A) Teaching a lesson
B) Congregational prayer
C) Quran recitation
D) Any purpose

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the mosque is crowded, prayer takes precedence over all other acts, and structural changes to mosques must align with their primary purpose of prayer.

Teaching and Disciplining Children in the Mosque
Middle part of passage on teaching and disciplining children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on teaching Quran to children for pay in the mosque and identify the intra-madhhab difference regarding teaching in a shop in the mosque courtyard.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran to children for a fee in the mosque is sinful; without pay it is permissible, but the hadith advises keeping children away.

This part tackles the sensitive issue of using the mosque for educating children. While teaching adults is permissible, children and paid instruction raise concerns. There is also a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding teaching in a shop in the mosque courtyard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act of teaching children Quran in the mosque
The text states it is not permissible (la yajuz) and sinful (ya'tham) when done for pay. Without pay, it is permissible (yajuz).
2
Note the hadith cited
The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Keep your children and madmen away from your mosques.' This supports the dislike of children in mosques.
3
Distinguish the ruling on disciplining children
Disciplining (ta'dib) children in the mosque is not permissible if done for pay, but is permissible without pay.
4
Recognize the dispute on teaching in a shop in the mosque courtyard
According to Abu Hanifa, teaching in a shop in the mosque courtyard is not permissible. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible if it does not harm the public.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له متاع في المسجد يخاف عليه فإنه يتيمم ويدخل في الصلاة، وإذا ضاق المسجد كان للمصلي أن يزعج القاعد من موضعه ليصلي فيه وإن كان مشتغلاً بالذكر أو الدرس أو قراءة القرآن أو الاعتكاف وكذا لأهل المحلة أن يمنعوا من ليس منهم عن فيه إذا ضاق بهم المسجد. أهل المحلة قسموا المسجد وضربوا فيه حائطاً ولكل منهم إمام على حدة ومؤذنهم واحد لا بأس به، والأولى أن يكون لكل طائفة مؤذن كما يجوز لأهل المحلة أن يجعلوا المسجد الواحد مسجدين فلهم أن يجعلوا المسجدين واحداً لإقامة الجماعة أما للتذكير أو للتدريس فلا لأنه ما بنى له وإن جاز فيه. وفي شرح الآثار أن البيع وخصف النعل وإنشاد الشعر مما كان لا هذا غير مكروه، وما يعمه منه أو يغلبه فمكروه. ويجوز الدرس في المسجد وإن كان فيه استعمال اللبود والبواري المسبلة لأجل المسجد، لو علم الصبيان القرآن في المسجد لا يجوز ويأثم، وكذا التأديب فيه أي لا يجوز التأديب فيه إذا كان بأجر، وينبغي أن يجوز بغير أجر، وأما الصبيان فقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «جنبوا مساجدكم صبيانكم ومجانينكم وكذا لا يجوز التعليم في دكان في فناء المسجد؛ هذا عند أبي حنيفة . وعندهما يجوز إذا لم يضر بالعامة . أصابه البرد الشديد في الطريق فدخل مسجداً فيه خشب الغير ولو لم يوقد ناراً يهلك فخشب المسجد في الإيقاد أولى من غيره، يجوز إدخال الحبوب وأثاث البيت في المسجد للخوف في الفتنة العامة .اهـ وفيها من الوقف : اتخذا مسجداً على أنه بالخيار جاز المسجد والشرط باطل جعل وسط داره مسجداً وأذن للناس في الدخول يعم المسجد من وقد خالف فيه قاضيخان كما مر فتدبر اهـ. ويؤيده قول الإسعاف لأنه لا بد من التأبيد والتوقيت
If he has property in the mosque that he fears for, he may perform tayammum and enter the prayer. And if the mosque is crowded, the worshiper may displace the sitting person from his place to pray, even if he is engaged in dhikr, lesson, Quran recitation, or i'tikaf. Similarly, the people of the neighborhood may prevent those who are not from among them from entering when the mosque is crowded. The people of the neighborhood divided the mosque and built a wall in it, each having a separate imam and a single mu'adhdhin; there is nothing wrong with it, and it is better that each group has its own mu'adhdhin. Waqf: Condition of Option and Necessity
Final part of passage on waqf and necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a condition of option (khiyar) in making a mosque is void while the mosque itself is valid, and apply the rule of necessity to using mosque property.

Core Idea
A mosque made with a condition of option is valid, but the condition is void because waqf requires perpetuity; necessity permits using mosque wood to save a life.

The final part addresses two important waqf-related rulings: the validity of a mosque if the founder stipulates an option to revoke, and the permissibility of using mosque property (wood) in case of life-threatening cold. The principle of perpetuity (ta'bid) is central.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on making a mosque with a condition of option
The text states: if two people take a place as a mosque on the condition that they have an option, the mosque is valid and the condition is void.
2
Understand the principle of perpetuity (ta'bid) in waqf
Waqf requires permanence; a condition of option contradicts this, so the condition is invalid.
3
Analyze the necessity case: using mosque wood for heating
If a person is in danger of freezing and enters a mosque containing wood, the wood of the mosque is more appropriate for lighting than other wood, even if the wood is waqf.
4
Note the difference of opinion (Qadikhan)
Qadikhan had a differing view on whether permission to enter applies to all, but the author supports the view that perpetuity is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
التأبيد (al-Ta'bid): Perpetuity - the requirement that a waqf be permanent and not temporary.
الخيار (al-Khiyar): Option or right to annul the act of making a mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on using mosque wood to light a fire when someone will otherwise die from extreme cold?
A) Not permissible because it is waqf property.
B) Permissible and the mosque's wood is more appropriate than other wood.
C) Permissible only if the wood is not dedicated.
D) Not permissible unless the mosque authorities permit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, waqf requires perpetuity (ta'bid), so a condition of option is void, but necessity can override property rules to preserve life.
